Intel presently considers the following to be important factors that could cause actual results to differ materially from the company&#8217;s expectations.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; font-size:10pt;"><tr><td style="width:48px;"></td><td></td></tr><tr><td style="vertical-align:top"><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:12pt;padding-left:24px;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">&#8226;</font></div></td><td style="vertical-align:top;"><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">Demand for Intel's products is highly variable and, in recent years, Intel has experienced declining orders in the traditional PC market segment. Demand could be different from Intel's expectations due to factors including changes in business and economic conditions; consumer confidence or income levels; customer acceptance of Intel&#8217;s and competitors&#8217; products; competitive and pricing pressures, including actions taken by competitors; supply constraints and other disruptions affecting customers; changes in customer order patterns including order cancellations; and changes in the level of inventory at customers.</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div></td></tr></table><table cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" style="font-family:Times New Roman; consistent with expectations, demonstrating financial growth and a solid start to the year.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">First-quarter revenue of </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$12.8B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">&#32;was consistent with our expectations and up </font><font Gross margin of 60% was down two points from the fourth quarter and one point above our guidance driven by lower factory startup on 14nm and other non-production cost of sales. Spending came in at </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$4.9B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, $100M above the prior outlook driven primarily by a current-period charge related to ongoing litigation. Operating income for the first quarter was </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$2.5B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, up </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">1%</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">&#32;from a year ago. Earnings per share was </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">38 cents</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">. As we look forward to the second quarter of 2014, we are forecasting the midpoint of the revenue range at </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$13.0B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, up 2% from the first quarter. This forecast is in line with the average seasonal increase for the second quarter. We are forecasting the midpoint of the gross margin range for the second quarter to be </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">63 percent</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, a three point increase from the first quarter. This is primarily driven by lower factory start-up costs as we ramp 14nm, higher platform* volumes, and lower platform* write-offs as we qualify the first 14nm products. This is partially offset by the increase in tablet volume and the related contra revenue dollars. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;font-weight:bold;">Spending</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">Spending for R&amp;D and MG&amp;A for the year is expected to be </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$18.9B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, plus or minus </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$200M</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">, higher than our prior expectation of $18.6B.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">Amortization of acquisition-related intangibles is forecast to be approximately </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$300M</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">&#32;for 2014, unchanged from prior expectations.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">Depreciation for the year is still forecast to be approximately </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">$7.4B</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">.</font></div><br><div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">*PC Client Group and Data Center Group microprocessors and chipsets</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;"><br></font></div></div><hr style="page-break-after:always"><a name="s307C50C24A1F32D58699D0A4405CAD74"></a><div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:right;font-size:10pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">Page </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:10pt;">5</font></div></div><br><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;font-weight:bold;">Other Income Statement Items</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">The tax rate for each of the remaining quarters of 2014 is still expected to be </font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">27%</font><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">.</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;font-weight:bold;">Balance Sheet and Cash Flow Items</font></div><div style="line-height:120%;text-align:left;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;">Capital spending is forecast to be $11.0B plus or minus $500M, approximately flat to 2013, unchanged from prior forecast. </font></div><div style="line-height:120%;font-size:12pt;"><font style="font-family:inherit;font-size:12pt;"><br></font></div><div
